  (function() {
    var jdgmThemeFixes = null;
    if (!jdgmThemeFixes) return;
    var thisThemeFix = jdgmThemeFixes[Shopify.theme.id];
    if (!thisThemeFix) return;

his CSS snippet uses the @font-face rule to load various weights and styles of the Poppins font from a specific CDN. Each @font-face block defines a unique combination of font-family, font-weight, font-style, and font-display, with corresponding font file URLs for different formats (woff2 and woff).
Key Components:
Font-Family: Specifies the name of the font (Poppins in this case).
Font-Weight and Font-Style:
font-weight: Defines the thickness of the font (e.g., 400, 500, 600).
font-style: Specifies whether the font is normal or italic.
Font-Display: Indicates how the font is displayed while loading. swap ensures the text is displayed using a fallback font until the custom font loads.
Source URLs (src):
Includes links to the font files (woff2 for modern browsers, woff for compatibility).
Includes additional query parameters (hmac, h1 to h7) likely for validation or CDN-specific configuration.
This reduces load time if the font is already installed on the user's system.
Subset Fonts: If your application doesn't require all characters (e.g., specific language subsets), consider serving a subset of the font for faster loading.
Combine Similar Styles: To minimize redundant @font-face declarations, combine weights or styles where possible.

he JavaScript and HTML code you provided appears to be part of a webpage implementation for managing product interactions, such as quick view, compare, and adding to the wishlist or cart. Here's an explanation of some key parts of the code:
JavaScript Explanation:
Responsive Handling:
The script checks the viewport width (window.innerWidth) to adjust the loading attribute of images based on screen size. For example, it sets images with loading="lazy" to loading="eager" when the viewport is smaller than 768px (mobile screens) and vice versa for larger screens.
Lazy Loading:
The script uses the lazyload class to handle lazy loading of images. It updates the src attribute of images dynamically when the images are within the visible viewport and meets certain conditions. This helps improve the page load time by deferring the loading of images that are not visible initially.
Template Fetching:
The script fetches a template for product configuration and quick view functionality based on the product URL. It checks if the quickviewId or quickshopId is set in the T4Srequest object and fetches the template accordingly. The fetched template might be used to display a modal for quick product interactions.
Event Handling:
There are functions to open and close modals or pop-ups, as well as managing the visibility of certain UI elements (e.g., quick view buttons or compare buttons).
Session Storage:
sessionStorage is used to store the quickviewId and quickshopId, which can be accessed across page reloads within the same session. This allows for managing states like which modal or item is being viewed or interacted with.
HTML Template Explanation:
Product Buttons Template (btns_pr_temp):
A series of action buttons for each product are defined. These include:
Quick view (t4s-pr-quickview)
Compare (t4s-pr-compare)
Add to Wishlist (t4s-pr-wishlist)
Add to Cart (t4s-pr-addtocart)
These buttons use SVG icons and text to provide interactivity for users.
Modal Template (t4s_temp_modal):
Defines a modal structure that is used for showing additional details about products when the user clicks on a quick view button. The modal can be closed using the close button (t4s-modal-close).
PhotoSwipe Template (photoswipe_template):
This template is used for displaying product images in a full-screen gallery or lightbox. The gallery supports multiple images and allows for actions such as zoom, share, and fullscreen view.
Cart and Navigation Templates:
Templates for cart interactions (t4s-mini_cart) and a mobile drawer for the menu (t4s-menu-drawer) are included, which help in managing user navigation and cart functionality in a responsive manner.
CSS Links:
There are several external CSS stylesheets being linked for the styling of mobile navigation, cart buttons, and custom effects. These stylesheets ensure that the UI elements are styled correctly across different devices.
Use Cases:
Quick View and Product Interaction: The Quick view button template is likely part of the product cards where users can see product details in a modal without leaving the page. Similarly, the Add to Cart button would allow users to add items to their cart.
Lazy Loading: The code ensures that images only load when they are about to be viewed by the user, which can improve performance and reduce initial page load time.
Mobile and Desktop Optimizations: Different image loading strategies and drawer-based navigation are optimized for mobile and desktop views.

It seems that you are enabling functionality for product options (e.g., size variations like "Ash / M", and the ability to select different sizes).
Product Variants and Quantity Selector:
The product has variants (size options like "Ash / M", "Ash / L") displayed using a dropdown. Some of the variants are out of stock and are marked as "disabled".
A quantity selector allows the user to select how many items they want to add to their cart, with limits (1-5 items).
Recommendations:
Accessibility:

For the accessibility of buttons (like the search and account icon), consider adding aria-label attributes that provide descriptive text for screen readers.
Example: <button aria-label="Open search" class="t4s-toolbar-icon">...</button>
Responsive Design:

Ensure that the sticky add-to-cart button and other elements adjust properly for mobile devices. For instance, you could hide certain components on small screens or make the layout adapt to smaller viewports.
Error Handling for Product Variants:
If a user selects an out-of-stock variant, you could show a more prominent message explaining that the variant is unavailable. This will help avoid confusion when interacting with the dropdown options.
JS and Event Handling:
Ensure that JavaScript handles interactions correctly, especially for things like toggling the "Back to Top" button visibility based on scroll position, and updating the cart when the quantity or variant changes.
Performance:
Consider lazy loading images to improve page load times, especially for the product images inside the sticky add-to-cart section, as they're critical for the user's shopping experience.
Visual Enhancements:
Use CSS transitions or animations for the "Back to Top" button to make it appear/disappear smoothly as the user scrolls. Similarly, adding hover effects to buttons can enhance the user interface.
